Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two Mu'tazili interpretations of divine guidance and misguidance in the Quran. The author begins by affirming that God creates both guidance and misguidance directly, as indicated by the verse about expanding the chest for Islam or making it tight. He then refutes al-Ka'bi's claim that the verse refers to reward and punishment. Al-Ka'bi argued that if someone submits, God gives him special gifts as reward, and if someone disbelieves, God constricts his chest as punishment. The author rejects this as distortion, because the verse links the expansion or tightness of the chest directly to God's will, not to a person's prior action. In the source text, God attributes Islam to the person when He expands the chest, and disbelief when He makes the heart tight, not the reverse. Al-Ka'bi mistakenly reversed the causal relationship, making the ruling (Islam or disbelief) into a cause (reward or punishment) and the cause (divine action) into a ruling. Then the author refutes the Basrian view that 'guidance' means 'clarification' and 'misguidance' means 'naming'. This is refuted by a reductio ad absurdum: If guidance were merely clarification, and clarification is universal (reaches everyone), then every disbeliever would also receive the expansion of the chest (شرح الصدر) because they all receive clarification. Similarly, if misguidance were just naming, then the disbeliever would simultaneously have an expanded chest (due to receiving clarification) and a tight chest (due to being named misguided), which is impossible. Consequently, God's division of people into those with expanded chests and those with tight chests would be meaningless, since everyone would have an expanded chest. Attributing such an erroneous division to God is blasphemy. Finally, the author presents a dialectical argument: If the Mu'tazila say 'misguidance' in the verse means 'naming', then God's naming someone misguided must be an act of will. Then they are asked: Does God also will the actual misguidance of that person? If they say yes, they concede the Ash'ari position; if they say no, they face the contradiction that God wills to name someone misguided while willing them to be guided, which would mean the naming is false.

Misconception & Correction

What is the immediate contradictory consequence of the Basrian interpretation, according to Nasafi?
A) Disbelievers would have tight chests.
B) Believers would have tight chests.
C) Disbelievers would have expanded chests.
D) God would be unjust.

Key Takeaway
Interpreting guidance as clarification makes God's division of people into guided and misguided nonsensical and blasphemous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter verses that challenge your understanding of God's absolute control, like those on guidance and misguidance, do you feel tempted to reinterpret them to make them more palatable to human reason? Have you done so recently? Repent and submit to the plain meaning.
?
The Basrians were forced to choose: either admit that God wills misguidance (which they denied) or admit that His naming is false. Are you willing to accept hard theological truths even when they conflict with your previous assumptions? What assumption about God might you be clinging to that the Quran actually contradicts?
?
This passage calls attributing error to God in His division 'disbelief and misguidance'. Examine your heart: have you ever complained about God's decree, questioned His wisdom in guiding some and not others, or felt that His division is unfair? Confess that to yourself now, and ask Allah for protection from such thoughts.

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Interpretation of Noah's Verse
Refutation of Mu'tazilite interpretation of Noah's verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical flaw in the Mu'tazilite interpretation of the verse from Surah Hud 11:34 and how the author uses the verse to affirm that God genuinely wills to lead some astray.

Core Idea
If God cannot will misguidance, Noah's conditional becomes meaningless.

The Mu'tazilites argued that the verse 'if God intends to lead you astray' only states a hypothetical condition without affirming that God actually wills misguidance. In this passage, the author exposes the logical consequence of their view: if true, Noah's statement would always promise benefit, contradicting the fact that his advice was not benefiting his people. This refutation defends the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God genuinely wills both guidance and misguidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Mu'tazilite claim
Read the Arabic verse and note the Mu'tazilite claim that it only states a condition, not actual divine will.
2
Follow the logical argument
The author argues: if God's willing misguidance is impossible, then the condition can never be true, so Noah would be asserting that his advice always profits them.
This is a conditional with an impossible condition.
3
Check the context
The context shows Noah was despairing and his advice was not profiting them, so the condition must be real.
The verse is a complaint, not a hypothetical.
4
Conclude the refutation
Therefore, the Mu'tazilite interpretation is invalid; God's will to misguide is affirmed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال تعالى خبرًا عن نوح عليه السلام حيث قال لقومه: ﴿ وَلَا يَنفَعُكُمْ نُصْحِي إِنْ أَرَدتُ أَنْ أَنصَحَ لَكُمْ إِن كَانَ اللهُ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ ذكر أن الله يريد أن يغوي الكفرة، وتأويل المعتزلة أن في الآية أن نصحة لا ينفع إن كان الله يريد أن يغويهم وليس فيه أنه يريد، تأويل فاسد، لأنه إذا كان يستحيل منه إرادة غوايتهم أي فائدة في ذكر الآية على الأمر، لو كان كما يزعمون لكان ينبغي أن يكون مراد نوح عليه السلام من هذه الآية بيان أن نصحه ينفعهم لا محالة، لأن فيه تعليق نفي نفع النصح بما يستحيل ثبوته وهو إرادة إغوائهم، وتعليق النفي بما يستحيل ثبوته يكون تأكيدًا للإثبات، ويصير كأنه قال: لا ينفعكم نصحي، إذا كان الله يريد أن يغويكم فإذا استحال أن يريد أن يغويكم ينفعكم نصحي وحيث رأينا أنه كان لا ينفعهم وإنما قال ذلك يأسا من نفع نصحه لهم عند إرادة الله أن يغويهم، فكان ذلك دليلاً على فساد التأويل. وما قاله جعفر بن حرب أن الآية تدل أنه كان في قوم نوح عليه السلام قوم مجبرة يقولون: إن الله تعالى يريد الفساد فخاطبهم منبها لهم على بطلان قولهم فقال: وَلَا يَنفَعُكُمْ نُصْحِي إِنْ أَرَدتُ أَنْ أَنصَحَ لَكُمْ فيما أدعوكم إن كان الأمر كما ذكرتم من أنه تعالى المريد لفسادكم ويخلق الكفر فيكم. فاسد، لأن الأمر لو كان كما زعم
And the Exalted said, reporting from Noah, peace be upon him, when he said to his people: 'And my advice will not profit you, if I intend to advise you, if God intends to lead you astray (yughwiyakum).' He mentions that God intends to lead the disbelievers astray. The interpretation of the Mu'tazilites is that in the verse, his advice does not profit if God intends to lead them astray, and it does not mention that He intends [it]. [This is] an invalid interpretation, because if His willing their going-astray is impossible for Him, what benefit is there in mentioning the verse concerning the matter? If it were as they claim, then the intent of Noah, peace be upon him, from this verse should have been to clarify that his advice profits them necessarily, because it suspends the negation of the profit of advice upon something whose existence is impossible, namely His willing their going-astray, and suspending negation upon what is impossible is an affirmation of affirmation, and it becomes as if he said: 'My advice will not profit you, if God intends to lead you astray, and if it is impossible that He intends to lead you astray, then my advice profits you.' But we see that it was not profiting them, and he only said that out of despair of the profit of his advice to them when God intends to lead them astray, so that was evidence of the corruption of the interpretation. And what Ja'far ibn Ḥarb said—that the verse indicates that among the people of Noah, peace be upon him, there were a people of the compulsionists (mujbira) who say that God, the Exalted, intends corruption, so he addressed them, alerting them to the falsehood of their statement, saying: 'And my advice will not profit you, if I intend to advise you, in what I call you to, if the matter is as you mentioned that He, the Exalted, is the willer of your corruption and creates disbelief in you'—is invalid, because the matter, if it were as he claimed...
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two interpretations of the verse from Sūrat Hūd (11:34) where Noah tells his people that his advice will not benefit them if God intends to lead them astray (yughwiyahum). The author first refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation, which claims that the verse only states a conditional (if God intended) but does not affirm that God actually intends misguidance. The author argues that if God's willing misguidance is impossible, the conditional becomes meaningless; Noah would be saying his advice profits them necessarily (since the condition can never be fulfilled). But the context shows Noah was despairing, and that his advice was indeed not profiting them because God willed to lead them astray. Therefore, the Mu'tazilite interpretation is invalid. The author then refutes Ja'far ibn Ḥarb's alternative reading, which claims the verse was directed at a group of 'mujbira' (compulsionists) among Noah's people who believed God wills corruption. Ja'far argued that Noah was hypothetically addressing their claim. The author dismisses this as invalid, but the passage is cut off mid-sentence; the argument likely would show that this interpretation also fails because it misrepresents the verse's intent.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse only states a hypothetical condition without affirming that God actually wills misguidance.
Correction: The author shows that if it were only hypothetical, Noah would be promising benefit, but he was despairing, so it must be real.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the Mu'tazilite interpretation that the verse about Noah only states a condition (if God intends) but does not affirm that God actually intends misguidance?
A) Because Noah's advice actually benefited his people.
B) Because if God's willing misguidance is impossible, the conditional would make Noah's advice always beneficial, contradicting the fact that it was not benefiting them.
C) Because the verse explicitly says God does not intend misguidance.
D) Because the Mu'tazilites misinterpret the word 'yughwiyakum'.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite interpretation fails because it would make Noah's statement a promise of benefit, contradicting the context of despair.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses like Hud 11:34, do you trust the plain meaning or do you find yourself rationalizing to fit your own assumptions about God's justice? In what specific area of your faith have you fallen into the Mu'tazilite trap of intellectualizing away clear divine attributes?
?
Noah's despair reveals that even the most sincere da'wah fails without God's will. How does this humble your own efforts in calling others to Islam? Are you willing to accept that success is entirely from God, not your eloquence or strategy?
?
The Mu'tazilites wanted to protect God's mercy by denying His will to misguide, but in doing so, they undermined the Quranic text. Are there places in your life where you twist the truth to avoid an uncomfortable theological implication? Will you submit to the Quran even when it clashes with your reason?

Refuting Ja'far ibn Ḥarb's Interpretation of Noah's Verse
Refutation of Ja'far ibn Ḥarb's alternative interpretation of Noah's verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ja'far ibn Ḥarb's alternative interpretation of the verse and the author's initial refutation, though the argument is incomplete due to a page break.

Core Idea
Ja'far ibn Ḥarb claimed the verse was addressed to compulsionists among Noah's people.

Ja'far ibn Ḥarb, a Mu'tazilite theologian, proposed that the verse was not about God's actual will but was a hypothetical addressing those who believed God coerces disbelief (mujbira). The author begins a refutation but the text breaks off. This lesson explores what we have and encourages reflection on how the author would complete the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read Ja'far's claim
Understand that Ja'far says the verse targets compulsionists who think God wills corruption, and Noah hypothetically addresses their claim.
2
Examine the author's response
The author says the claim is invalid, but the argument is cut off mid-sentence.

3

Consider what the author might have said: perhaps that Ja'far's interpretation also avoids the plain meaning or leads to a similar flaw.
This incomplete passage is marked for review.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال تعالى خبرًا عن نوح عليه السلام حيث قال لقومه: ﴿ وَلَا يَنفَعُكُمْ نُصْحِي إِنْ أَرَدتُ أَنْ أَنصَحَ لَكُمْ إِن كَانَ اللهُ يُرِيدُ أَن يُغْوِيَكُمْ ﴾ ذكر أن الله يريد أن يغوي الكفرة، وتأويل المعتزلة أن في الآية أن نصحة لا ينفع إن كان الله يريد أن يغويهم وليس فيه أنه يريد، تأويل فاسد، لأنه إذا كان يستحيل منه إرادة غوايتهم أي فائدة في ذكر الآية على الأمر، لو كان كما يزعمون لكان ينبغي أن يكون مراد نوح عليه السلام من هذه الآية بيان أن نصحه ينفعهم لا محالة، لأن فيه تعليق نفي نفع النصح بما يستحيل ثبوته وهو إرادة إغوائهم، وتعليق النفي بما يستحيل ثبوته يكون تأكيدًا للإثبات، ويصير كأنه قال: لا ينفعكم نصحي، إذا كان الله يريد أن يغويكم فإذا استحال أن يريد أن يغويكم ينفعكم نصحي وحيث رأينا أنه كان لا ينفعهم وإنما قال ذلك يأسا من نفع نصحه لهم عند إرادة الله أن يغويهم، فكان ذلك دليلاً على فساد التأويل. وما قاله جعفر بن حرب أن الآية تدل أنه كان في قوم نوح عليه السلام قوم مجبرة يقولون: إن الله تعالى يريد الفساد فخاطبهم منبها لهم على بطلان قولهم فقال: وَلَا يَنفَعُكُمْ نُصْحِي إِنْ أَرَدتُ أَنْ أَنصَحَ لَكُمْ فيما أدعوكم إن كان الأمر كما ذكرتم من أنه تعالى المريد لفسادكم ويخلق الكفر فيكم. فاسد، لأن الأمر لو كان كما زعم
And the Exalted said, reporting from Noah, peace be upon him, when he said to his people: 'And my advice will not profit you, if I intend to advise you, if God intends to lead you astray (yughwiyakum).' He mentions that God intends to lead the disbelievers astray. The interpretation of the Mu'tazilites is that in the verse, his advice does not profit if God intends to lead them astray, and it does not mention that He intends [it]. [This is] an invalid interpretation, because if His willing their going-astray is impossible for Him, what benefit is there in mentioning the verse concerning the matter? If it were as they claim, then the intent of Noah, peace be upon him, from this verse should have been to clarify that his advice profits them necessarily, because it suspends the negation of the profit of advice upon something whose existence is impossible, namely His willing their going-astray, and suspending negation upon what is impossible is an affirmation of affirmation, and it becomes as if he said: 'My advice will not profit you, if God intends to lead you astray, and if it is impossible that He intends to lead you astray, then my advice profits you.' But we see that it was not profiting them, and he only said that out of despair of the profit of his advice to them when God intends to lead them astray, so that was evidence of the corruption of the interpretation. And what Ja'far ibn Ḥarb said—that the verse indicates that among the people of Noah, peace be upon him, there were a people of the compulsionists (mujbira) who say that God, the Exalted, intends corruption, so he addressed them, alerting them to the falsehood of their statement, saying: 'And my advice will not profit you, if I intend to advise you, in what I call you to, if the matter is as you mentioned that He, the Exalted, is the willer of your corruption and creates disbelief in you'—is invalid, because the matter, if it were as he claimed...
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two interpretations of the verse from Sūrat Hūd (11:34) where Noah tells his people that his advice will not benefit them if God intends to lead them astray (yughwiyahum). The author first refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation, which claims that the verse only states a conditional (if God intended) but does not affirm that God actually intends misguidance. The author argues that if God's willing misguidance is impossible, the conditional becomes meaningless; Noah would be saying his advice profits them necessarily (since the condition can never be fulfilled). But the context shows Noah was despairing, and that his advice was indeed not profiting them because God willed to lead them astray. Therefore, the Mu'tazilite interpretation is invalid. The author then refutes Ja'far ibn Ḥarb's alternative reading, which claims the verse was directed at a group of 'mujbira' (compulsionists) among Noah's people who believed God wills corruption. Ja'far argued that Noah was hypothetically addressing their claim. The author dismisses this as invalid, but the passage is cut off mid-sentence; the argument likely would show that this interpretation also fails because it misrepresents the verse's intent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The author instantly dismisses Ja'far's interpretation as invalid. How quickly do you reject interpretations of the Quran that go against the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah? Test yourself: have you ever entertained an opinion that made God's decree easier for you to accept, rather than humbling yourself before His absolute will?

The Meaning of God's Will: Refuting Compulsion
Al-Nasafi questions the meaning of 'will of compulsion' and refutes Abu al-Hudhayl's coercive interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu al-Hudhayl's interpretation of divine will as coercive creation of faith is inconsistent with Mu'tazilite principles.

Core Idea
If God created faith by force, He would be the believer, not humans.

Al-Nasafi begins by asking the Mu'tazilites what they mean by 'will of compulsion.' Abu al-Hudhayl's answer reduces God's will to an act of coercion. But this contradicts the Mu'tazilites' own doctrine that each person is the agent of their own actions. If God directly creates faith in a person, then God becomes the believer, rendering human faith meaningless.

Guided Path
1
Understand the question
Al-Nasafi asks the Mu'tazilites to clarify their concept of the will of compulsion. Notice how the question itself challenges their position.
The phrase 'mashi'at al-qasr wa al-jabr' is key.
2
Identify Abu al-Hudhayl's claim
Identify his interpretation: God creates faith in people by force without their choice, making them believers against their will.
3
Recall the Mu'tazilite principle
The Mu'tazilites hold that each human is the doer of their own faith or disbelief, and God does not create human actions. Grasp this because it is the basis of the refutation.
This principle is stated in the passage: 'the believer is the doer of faith'.
4
Apply the principle to the claim
If God created faith in someone, then according to their own logic, God would be the believer, not the person. This would invalidate the Quranic verses about God guiding all.
Notice the use of the verses: 'If He willed, He would guide you all'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجواب عنه أن نقول : أيش تعنون بمشيئة القصر والجبر؟ فتفرقوا عند ذلك في تفسيرها، فزعم أبو الهذيل ومن تابعه أن تفسير ذلك بأن يخلق فيهم الإيمان جبرا بدون اختيارهم فيوجد فيهم الإيمان ويندفع الكفر.
قيل لهم: إن من مذهبكم أن المؤمن هو فاعل الإيمان والكافر هو فاعل الكفر، ولهذا أبيتم أن يكون الله تعالى خالقًا لأفعال الخلق لأنه لو كان خالقا لكان هو المؤمن الكافر المطيع العاصي المصلي الصائم، فعلى هذا لو خلق فيهم الإيمان لكان هو المؤمن لا العباد فلا يتصور إيمانهم ولم تنفذ مشيئة فبطل قوله: ﴿فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ﴾ وقوله: ﴿وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا﴾ إذ له قدرة جعل نفسه مؤمنًا لا قدرة جعل الكافر مؤمنًا وكذا ما اندفع عنه العجز عن جعل الكافر مؤمناً بل له القدرة على جعل نفسه مؤمنًا فلو شاء لأمن بنفسه وأتى نفسه هداها لا غير، ومن العجب العجيب أنه لو خلق في العبد إيمانا كسبا له باختياره وتعلقت قدرته به لم يكن العبد مؤمناً بل كان الله تعالى به مؤمنًا، لأنه هو الذي أوجد الإيمان ولو خلق فيه إيمانا وهدى بلا اختيار من جهة العبد ولا اكتساب ولا تعلق قدرته به لكان العبد مؤمناً، ولو كان الله تعالى أشرك المعتزلة في ربوبيته وفوض إليهم نصب أدلة دينه وعلق ذلك باختيارهم فأوجب على جميع الأمم الانقياد إليهم والرضا لصنيعهم والقبول لتحكمهم لكان الأولى بهم أن يستحيوا عن مثل هذا الكلام ونصب مثل هذا الدليل، فكيف ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك
The answer to it is that we say: What do you mean by the will of limitation and compulsion? So they differed at that point in its interpretation. Abu al-Hudhayl and those who followed him claimed that its interpretation is that He creates faith in them by compulsion without their choice, so faith occurs in them and disbelief is repelled. It was said to them: From your doctrine is that the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief, and because of this you refused that Allah be the creator of the actions of creation, because if He were the creator, He would be the believer, the disbeliever, the obedient, the disobedient, the one who prays, the one who fasts. Therefore, if He created faith in them, He would be the believer, not the servants, so their faith is inconceivable and the will would not be executed, so His statement: {If He willed, He would guide you all} and His statement: {And if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance} would become invalid, since He has the power to make Himself a believer, not the power to make the disbeliever a believer. Likewise, inability to make the disbeliever a believer is repelled from Him, rather He has the power to make Himself a believer. So if He willed, He would believe Himself and give Himself its guidance, nothing else. And from the strange wonder is that if He created in the servant faith as an acquisition for him by his choice and his power was attached to it, the servant would not be a believer, rather Allah would be a believer through it, because He is the one who brought faith into existence. And if He created in him faith and guidance without choice on the part of the servant, nor acquisition, nor attachment of his power to it, the servant would be a believer. And if Allah had associated the Mu'tazilites in His lordship and delegated to them the erection of proofs of His religion and attached that to their choice, and obligated all nations to submit to them, be satisfied with their action, and accept their arbitrary judgment, then it would be more fitting for them to be ashamed of such speech and the erection of such a proof. How [could that be], when none of that has occurred?
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Abu al-Hudhayl's interpretation of the divine will of compulsion (mashi'at al-jabr). Al-Nasafi begins by asking the Mu'tazilites: 'What do you mean by the will of limitation and compulsion?' He then notes that they differed in their interpretation. Abu al-Hudhayl claimed that God's will to guide all people means He creates faith in them by force without their choice. Al-Nasafi then turns the argument against them: according to Mu'tazilite doctrine, the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief. They even deny that God creates human actions, because if He did, He would be the doer of those actions. So if God were to create faith in a person directly, He would become the believer, not the person. This contradicts the verses that say God could guide all, because He would then be guiding Himself, not others. Al-Nasafi then presents a paradoxical consequence: if God created faith in a person as an acquisition by the person's own power, then according to their logic, the person would not be the believer—God would be. But if God created faith without any involvement of the person's power, then the person would be a believer. This reveals an inconsistency in their position. He ends with a sarcastic remark: if the Mu'tazilites were truly delegated by God to set up proofs, they should be ashamed of such weak arguments.

Key Terms
مشيئة الجبر
الإيمان
الكفر
أبو الهذيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's will to guide all means He creates faith in people by force, making them believers without their choice.
Correction: If God created faith by force, He would be the agent of that faith, making Him the believer, not the person. This contradicts the Quranic verses that imply guidance is given to others.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite principle mentioned in the text, who is the doer of faith?
A) God
B) The believer himself
C) Both God and the believer
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Hudhayl's interpretation is self-defeating because it violates the Mu'tazilite principle that each person is the agent of their own faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that God does not force faith upon you, how do you personally respond to the Quranic call to believe? Are you actively choosing faith, or are you passively waiting for a miraculous change? What specific step can you take today to demonstrate that your belief is your own choice?
?
If your disbelief or disobedience is genuinely your own doing (as this passage implies), how does that affect your sense of accountability before God? Does this burden feel heavy or freeing? What changes in your daily habits might this realization demand?
?
The Mu'tazilite argument reveals that if God created your actions, He would be the doer, not you. When you perform a good deed, do you often credit yourself or forget God's role? Reflect on a recent good deed: how can you acknowledge it as both your action and a gift from God, without falling into either extreme of self-praise or fatalism?

The Paradox of Compulsion and Human Agency
Al-Nasafi presents a paradox and uses satire to refute Abu al-Hudhayl's interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the paradoxical consequences of the coercive view and how Al-Nasafi uses satire to expose its absurdity.

Core Idea
If God creates faith without human agency, the person is a believer; with agency, God is the believer.

Al-Nasafi continues his refutation by presenting a strange contradiction. If God creates faith in a person as an acquisition by the person's own power, then according to Mu'tazilite logic, God would be the believer. But if God creates faith without any human involvement, then the person is the believer. This exposes the flaw in their reasoning. He concludes with a sarcastic remark about the Mu'tazilites' arrogance.

Guided Path
1
Read the paradox carefully
Al-Nasafi presents two scenarios. In the first, God creates faith as an acquisition by the person's choice. In the second, God creates faith without any human involvement. Notice the different outcomes.
Focus on the phrases 'كسبا له باختياره' and 'بلا اختيار'.
2
Analyze the contradiction
According to Mu'tazilite logic, when God creates faith with human acquisition, the doer is God (since He created it), so the person is not the believer. But when God creates faith without any human role, the person is the believer. This is backwards from what we would expect.
This reveals an inconsistency in their position.
3
Understand the sarcastic conclusion
Al-Nasafi imagines if the Mu'tazilites were delegated by God to set up proofs. He says they should be ashamed of their weak arguments.
This is a rhetorical device to emphasize the weakness of their case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجواب عنه أن نقول : أيش تعنون بمشيئة القصر والجبر؟ فتفرقوا عند ذلك في تفسيرها، فزعم أبو الهذيل ومن تابعه أن تفسير ذلك بأن يخلق فيهم الإيمان جبرا بدون اختيارهم فيوجد فيهم الإيمان ويندفع الكفر.
قيل لهم: إن من مذهبكم أن المؤمن هو فاعل الإيمان والكافر هو فاعل الكفر، ولهذا أبيتم أن يكون الله تعالى خالقًا لأفعال الخلق لأنه لو كان خالقا لكان هو المؤمن الكافر المطيع العاصي المصلي الصائم، فعلى هذا لو خلق فيهم الإيمان لكان هو المؤمن لا العباد فلا يتصور إيمانهم ولم تنفذ مشيئة فبطل قوله: ﴿فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ﴾ وقوله: ﴿وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا﴾ إذ له قدرة جعل نفسه مؤمنًا لا قدرة جعل الكافر مؤمنًا وكذا ما اندفع عنه العجز عن جعل الكافر مؤمناً بل له القدرة على جعل نفسه مؤمنًا فلو شاء لأمن بنفسه وأتى نفسه هداها لا غير، ومن العجب العجيب أنه لو خلق في العبد إيمانا كسبا له باختياره وتعلقت قدرته به لم يكن العبد مؤمناً بل كان الله تعالى به مؤمنًا، لأنه هو الذي أوجد الإيمان ولو خلق فيه إيمانا وهدى بلا اختيار من جهة العبد ولا اكتساب ولا تعلق قدرته به لكان العبد مؤمناً، ولو كان الله تعالى أشرك المعتزلة في ربوبيته وفوض إليهم نصب أدلة دينه وعلق ذلك باختيارهم فأوجب على جميع الأمم الانقياد إليهم والرضا لصنيعهم والقبول لتحكمهم لكان الأولى بهم أن يستحيوا عن مثل هذا الكلام ونصب مثل هذا الدليل، فكيف ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to fully understand how your choices and God's will work together, do you find yourself falling into confusion or pride? Al-Nasafi's paradox exposes the absurdity of over-rationalizing divine decree. Will you humble yourself and accept that God's wisdom may appear contradictory to human logic, or will you insist on finding a rational explanation even if it leads to absurdity?
?
This paradox shows that if God creates your faith, He alone deserves the credit. Does your heart truly believe that your salvation is entirely from God, or do you secretly think your own choice or effort played a part? Take a moment to examine your gratitude and reliance on God alone.
?
Al-Nasafi mocks those who claim to be partners with God in setting up proofs. Where in your life do you act as if you can fully grasp God's ways and judge His actions by your own standards? Will you repent from that attitude and surrender to His absolute wisdom, even when it seems paradoxical?

Refuting al-Jubba'i: Faith is Not Necessitated by Knowledge
Al-Nasafi refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that God creates necessary knowledge to compel faith, using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Nasafi rejects al-Jubba'i's claim that necessary knowledge compels faith, and how Quranic verses demonstrate that faith depends on God's will, not on proof or knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge of truth does not force belief; faith requires God's will.

Al-Jubba'i, a leading Mu'tazili scholar, attempted to salvage the concept of compulsion by arguing that God creates necessary knowledge of Islam in people, which then leads them to faith. Al-Nasafi shows this is corrupt: knowledge and faith are distinct, and the Quran proves that even with undeniable proofs, people can refuse to believe. In this lesson, we will walk through his logical refutation and the scriptural evidence he brings.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the full translation to grasp al-Nasafi's argument flow.
Notice how al-Nasafi quotes multiple Quranic verses to support his point.
2
Understand al-Jubba'i's claim
Identify what al-Jubba'i said: that God creates necessary knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri) and proofs in the servant, so that they then believe. This is his interpretation of the 'will of compulsion'.
Al-Jubba'i tries to solve a problem in earlier determinist views.
3
Follow al-Nasafi's logical refutation
Al-Nasafi argues that knowledge of faith is other than faith itself; the existence of one does not necessitate the other. He then uses the Quranic verse about angels and the dead to show that even with all proofs, they would not believe unless God wills.
The key point: faith is a separate act of God's will, not a direct result of knowledge.
4
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Examine the two aspects al-Nasafi extracts from the verse, and then look at the additional verses (every sign, falling sky, recognition by People of the Book) that all confirm that people can have knowledge yet not believe.
These verses collectively prove that faith is not necessitated by knowledge or proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما رأى الجبائي عوار هذا الكلام وتشنيع أهل الحق عليهم زعم أن تفسير مشيئة الجبر أن يخلق الله تعالى في العبد العلم الضروري بصحة الإسلام وحقيقته ويقيم له الدلائل المثبتة له العلم الضروري بذلك فيؤمنوا حينئذ. وهذا فاسد لأن العلم بصحة الإيمان وحقيقة الدين غير الدين والإيمان، وليس من ضرورة وجود أحد المتغايرين وجود الآخر لا محالة، بل من الجائز أنه لا يوجد ألا ترى أن الله تعالى قال : ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّنَا نَزَّلْنَا إِلَيْهِمُ الْمَلَائِكَةَ وَكَلَّمَهُمُ الْمَوْتَى وَحَشَرْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ قُبُلًا مَّا كَانُوا لِيُؤْمِنُوا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ﴾ أخبر أنه وإن أقام كل دليل لا يؤمنون إلا أن يشاء الله تعالى إيمانهم فكان في الآية وجهان ينبئان عن بطلان هذا الكلام.
أحدهما أن قيام هذه الدلائل غير ومشيئة الإيمان غير حيث قال عز وجل: مَا كَانُوا لِيُؤْمِنُوا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ الله بعد وجود هذه الدلائل.
والآخر: أنه تعالى أثبت أن بقيام هذه الدلائل لا يؤمنون فثبت أن ليس من ضرورة ثبوت الدليل أو العلم به ثبوت الإيمان، وكذا قال : ﴿وَإِن يَرَوْا كُلَّ آيَةٍ لَا يُؤْمِنُوا بِهَا﴾ فمن قال يؤمنون بها محالة فقد كذب الله تعالى في خبره وقال تعالى: ﴿وَإِن يَرَوْا كِسْفًا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ سَاقِطًا يَقُولُوا سَحَابٌ مَرْكُومٌ﴾
يحققه : أن أهل العناد لم يكونوا يؤمنون وإن كان العلم بطريق الحقيقة ثابتا لهم كما قال تعالى: ﴿يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ وَإِنَّ فَرِيقًا مِّنْهُمْ لَيَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ﴾ .
فثبت أن وجود الإيمان والهداية ليس من ضرورة العلم والدليل
When al-Jubba'i saw the defect of this speech and the condemnation of the people of truth upon them, he claimed that the interpretation of the will of compulsion is that Allah creates in the servant necessary knowledge of the correctness of Islam and its truth, and establishes for him the proofs that confirm for him necessary knowledge of that, so they then believe. This is corrupt, because knowledge of the correctness of faith and the truth of religion is other than religion and faith, and from the necessity of the existence of one of two distinct things, the existence of the other is not inevitable; rather it is possible that it does not exist. Do you not see that Allah said: {And even if We sent down to them the angels and the dead spoke to them and We gathered before them everything face to face, they would not have believed unless Allah willed}? He informed that even if He established every proof, they would not believe unless Allah willed their faith. In the verse there are two aspects that indicate the invalidity of this speech. One of them: that the establishment of these proofs is other than the will of faith, where He said: {They would not have believed unless Allah willed} after the existence of these proofs. The other: that He, exalted, established that with the establishment of these proofs they do not believe, so it is established that the existence of faith is not a necessity of the existence of the proof or knowledge of it. Likewise He said: {And even if they see every sign, they would not believe in it}. So whoever says they would inevitably believe has lied against Allah in His report. And He said: {And if they see a fragment from the sky falling, they say: 'Piled-up clouds'}. He confirms it: that the people of obstinacy would not believe, even if knowledge of the truth was firmly established for them, as He said: {They recognize it as they recognize their own children, but indeed a group of them conceal the truth while they know}. So it is established that the existence of faith and guidance is not a necessity of knowledge and proof.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Jubba'i's alternative interpretation of the will of compulsion. Al-Jubba'i, seeing the weakness of Abu al-Hudhayl's view, claimed that God's will to guide means He creates necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī) in the servant about the truth of Islam, along with clear proofs, so that they then believe. Al-Nasafi dismisses this as corrupt. He argues that knowledge of faith is distinct from faith itself; the existence of one does not necessitate the other. To prove this, he quotes the Quranic verse: 'And even if We sent down to them the angels... they would not have believed unless Allah willed.' This verse shows two points: first, the proofs are distinct from God's will to create faith; second, even with all proofs, belief does not inevitably follow. He then cites other verses: 'And even if they see every sign, they would not believe in it,' and the verse about those who see a falling piece of sky and call it clouds, indicating their refusal despite clear evidence. Finally, he mentions the People of the Book who recognize the Prophet as they recognize their own children, yet conceal the truth knowingly. This establishes that faith and guidance are not necessitated by knowledge or proof alone.

Key Terms
العلم الضروري
مشيئة الجبر
الدليل
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That compelling evidence or necessary knowledge of the truth automatically leads to faith.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that knowledge and faith are distinct; Quranic verses prove that even with undeniable proofs, people can refuse to believe. Faith is solely by God's will.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'ولو أننا نزلنا إليهم الملائكة...' demonstrate according to al-Nasafi?
A) Faith is coerced through angels
B) Even after clear proofs, they would not believe unless God wills
C) The dead were brought to life for faith
D) Angels forced belief

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi proves that faith and guidance are not necessitated by knowledge or proof; they are subject to God's will alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If knowledge of the truth does not automatically lead to faith, what does that reveal about the condition of your own heart? Have you ever known something to be true from the Quran but felt a resistance in acting upon it? What does that resistance indicate about your dependence on God's will?
?
The People of the Book recognized the Prophet as they recognized their own children, yet they concealed the truth. Is there any truth from Allah that you are concealing from yourself or others—perhaps a sin you justify, a duty you neglect, or a responsibility you avoid? What would it take for you to stop relying on your own excuses and truly submit to God's will?
?
This lesson confronts you with the reality that faith is entirely in God's hands. Does this truth bring you humility or anxiety? When you have struggled with doubt or weak faith, have you sincerely turned to Allah asking Him to create faith in your heart, or have you relied solely on intellectual arguments? What is one concrete step you can take this week to humbly beg Allah for true iman?

Abu Hashim's Claim: Knowledge Does Not Force Belief
Abu Hashim's claim and initial refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu Hashim's reinterpretation of God's willing as creating necessary knowledge of punishment is flawed, and why such knowledge does not compel faith.

Core Idea
Knowing punishment does not force belief; obstinate people knew and still rejected.

Abu Hashim attempted to salvage his father's position by redefining God's will in terms of creating knowledge of punishment. This lesson examines his claim and the author's swift refutation using the examples of the obstinate and Iblis. You will see why mere knowledge does not necessitate belief.

Guided Path
1
Read Abu Hashim's claim
Read the passage where Abu Hashim states his interpretation of God's willing. Notice how he tries to avoid determinism.
2
Identify the refutation examples
The author cites the People of the Book and Iblis as counterexamples. Understand why these disprove Abu Hashim.
These figures knew their punishment but did not believe.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: If knowledge forced belief, everyone with proofs would believe. What does that say about human free will?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما رأى ابنه أبو هاشم فساد كلام أبيه زعم أن معنى مشيئة الجبران أن يخلق الله تعالى لهم العلم الضروري أنهم لو لم يؤمنوا لعذبوا عذابًا شديدا. وهذا أيضا فاسد لأن أهل العناد كانوا يعلمون أنهم يخلدون في النار بتكذيبه عليه السلام وما كانوا يؤمنون، وإبليس يعلم بذلك ولا يؤمن، فكذا من قامت له الدلائل الموجبة للعلم أو الذي خلق له العلم الضروري يعلم بذلك ولا يؤمن. ثم المذهب عنده أن الله تعالى يقدر على الظلم والسفه والكذب، ولو فعل شيئًا من ذلك لبطلت ألوهيته، ولا ضرر أعظم من زوال الربوبية وصيرورته عبدًا مربوبًا معاقبًا وهو يعلم أنه لو ظلم أو كذب أو سفه لتزول ربوبيته فكان على قضية كلامه مجبوراً على العدل والصدق والحكمة. وقد قررت الكلام فيه في مسألة خلق الأفعال ثم يقال له ولأبيه: هل بقيت معه قدرة الكفر بعد العلم الضروري بصحة الإيمان أو العلم أنه يعاقب؟ فإن قال: لا، قيل: كيف يؤمر بترك كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ وكيف يؤمر بالإيمان بدون القدرة إذ لو كانت قدرة الإيمان موجودة لكانت هي بعينها قدرة الكفر؟ وكيف يعاقب على كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ فإن قال: نعم. قيل: إذا كنت قدرة الكفر موجودة كان من الجائز أن يكفر بها ولا يؤمن. ثم الذي يبطل جميع تأويلاتهم أن الله تعالى قال : وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا وَلَكِنْ حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِنِّي لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ أخبر أنه تعالى لم يأت كل نفس هداها لما أن حق القول منه الأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ ولو أتى كل نفس
When his son Abu Hashim saw the falsity of his father's statement, he claimed that the meaning of 'willing' of the jabrians is that God Most High creates for them necessary knowledge that if they do not believe, they will be punished with a severe punishment. This is also false, because the obstinate people knew that they would abide forever in the Fire due to their denial of him (peace be upon him) and they would not believe, and Iblis knows that and does not believe. So likewise, the one for whom proofs necessitating knowledge are established, or the one for whom necessary knowledge has been created, knows that and does not believe. Then, according to him, the doctrine is that God Most High has power over injustice, foolishness, and lying. If He did any of that, His divinity would be invalidated. And there is no greater harm than the removal of lordship and his becoming a subjugated, punishable servant, while he knows that if He were unjust, lied, or acted foolishly, His lordship would be removed. So, according to the implication of his statement, He would be compelled to justice, truth, and wisdom. I have already discussed this in the issue of the creation of actions. Then it is said to him and his father: Does the power of disbelief remain with him after the necessary knowledge of the soundness of faith, or the knowledge that he will be punished? If he says: No, it is said: How can he be commanded to abandon disbelief which he has no power over? And how can he be commanded to believe without power, since if the power of faith existed, it would be the same as the power of disbelief? And how can he be punished for disbelief over which he has no power? If he says: Yes, it is said: If the power of disbelief exists, it is possible that he disbelieves with it and does not believe. Then that which invalidates all their interpretations is that God Most High said: 'And if We had willed, We could have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me will be fulfilled: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.' He informed that He Most High does not give every soul its guidance because the word from Him is 'I will surely fill Hell.' And if He gave every soul...
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage refutes Abu Hashim's alternative interpretation of God's 'willing' regarding faith. Abu Hashim claimed that God's will means He creates necessary knowledge in the disbeliever that if he does not believe, he will be severely punished. The author declares this false by pointing out that obstinate people (like the People of the Book) already knew they would be in the Fire for denying the Prophet, yet they did not believe, and Iblis knows this but does not believe. So knowledge of punishment does not necessitate faith. Next, the author notes Abu Hashim's own doctrine: that God has power over injustice, lying, etc., but if He did so, His divinity would be invalidated. The author argues that on Abu Hashim's premise, God would be compelled (mujbar) to be just, wise, etc., which contradicts the idea of free will. Then the author raises a dilemma: after necessary knowledge, does the ability (qudra) to disbelieve remain? If not, how can God command to abandon disbelief or punish for it? If yes, then the person might still disbelieve. Finally, the author presents the decisive refutation: Quran 32:13, where God states that if He willed, He could guide every soul, but His decree is to fill Hell. Thus, God does not give guidance to everyone, proving that necessary knowledge or proof does not force faith.

Key Terms
أبو هاشم
مشيئة
علم ضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God creates knowledge of punishment, the person has no choice but to believe.
Correction: The examples show that many had that knowledge yet freely chose disbelief.

Checkpoint
Who are the two examples the author uses to refute Abu Hashim's claim?
A) The Jews and Christians
B) The obstinate people and Iblis
C) The prophets and angels
D) The Jabriyya and Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
Necessary knowledge of punishment does not compel belief, as proven by the obstinate and Iblis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever known something was wrong (like a sin) and still done it? What does that reveal about the relationship between your knowledge and your faith? Are you willing to examine where your actions contradict your beliefs?
?
You know that Allah sees every action and that disobedience leads to punishment. In which area of your life do you act as if you don't have this knowledge? What would change if you truly internalized that knowledge does not save—only belief followed by action does?
?
Do you rely on your Islamic knowledge and proofs as a safety net, assuming that because you know the truth you are safe? This lesson shows that even Iblis knew. Where in your life is your knowledge not translating into obedience? How will you bridge that gap starting today?

The Compulsion of Justice: A Dilemma for Abu Hashim
Argument that Abu Hashim's view entails divine compulsion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author turns Abu Hashim's own doctrine against him, showing that God would be compelled to be just, which contradicts the idea of free will in divine actions.

Core Idea
Abu Hashim's view implies God is 'forced' to be just, which is incoherent.

The author now examines a consequence of Abu Hashim's theological framework. According to Abu Hashim, God has power over injustice, but if He did it, His divinity would cease. This leads to the implication that God is compelled to be just, a point the author uses to highlight the inconsistency in Abu Hashim's system.

Guided Path
1
Read Abu Hashim's doctrine
The passage states Abu Hashim's belief that God can do injustice, lying, etc., but doing so would destroy His divinity.
2
Follow the logical implication
If God knows that doing X would destroy His divinity, then He cannot freely do X. Thus He is compelled to do the opposite.
This resembles the Jabrite position Abu Hashim was trying to avoid.
3
Connect to the broader debate
Understand how this argument fits into the author's overall refutation of the Jabrite interpretation of will.
The author refers to a prior discussion on the creation of actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

When his son Abu Hashim saw the falsity of his father's statement, he claimed that the meaning of 'willing' of the jabrians is that God Most High creates for them necessary knowledge that if they do not believe, they will be punished with a severe punishment. This is also false, because the obstinate people knew that they would abide forever in the Fire due to their denial of him (peace be upon him) and they would not believe, and Iblis knows that and does not believe. The author argues that on Abu Hashim's premise, God would be compelled (mujbar) to be just, wise, etc., which contradicts the idea of free will. Then the author raises a dilemma: after necessary knowledge, does the ability (qudra) to disbelieve remain? If not, how can God command to abandon disbelief or punish for it? If yes, then the person might still disbelieve. Finally, the author presents the decisive refutation: Quran 32:13, where God states that if He willed, He could guide every soul, but His decree is to fill Hell. Thus, God does not give guidance to everyone, proving that necessary knowledge or proof does not force faith.

Key Terms

ظلم

كذب
ألوهية
ربوبية
جبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God has power over evil, He is free to do it; but the argument shows that such freedom would contradict His divinity.
Correction: Abu Hashim's claim that God can do evil but would lose divinity implies God is not free to do evil, contradicting the idea of absolute divine power.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about God's actions under Abu Hashim's framework?
A) God is completely free to do anything
B) God is compelled to be just, truthful, and wise
C) God is indifferent to justice
D) God has no power over injustice

Key Takeaway
Abu Hashim's view forces God to be 'compelled' to justice, which undermines the concept of divine free will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you believe that God could, in principle, commit injustice? If you say yes, what does that mean for your trust in His actions in your life? If you say no, does that mean God is compelled to be just, and how does that affect your understanding of His freedom?
?
This lesson argues that if God knows He would cease to be God by doing wrong, He is effectively forced to do right. In your own life, are there things you avoid not because you freely choose, but because the consequences would be unbearable? Does that make your choice less free? How does that parallel the dilemma presented here?
?
If God's justice is not a choice but a necessity of His nature, then can He truly be praised for being just? And if it is a choice, does that mean He could choose otherwise? What does your answer reveal about the tension between divine attributes and free will in your own heart?

The Dilemma of Power and the Decisive Quranic Proof
Dilemma and Quranic evidence for divine will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-part refutation: a logical dilemma about whether the disbeliever retains power to disbelieve after knowledge, and the Quranic verse that God does will some to be misguided.

Core Idea
Either the disbeliever has power or not; both options lead to contradictions, and the Quran settles it.

The author poses a critical dilemma to Abu Hashim and his father: after necessary knowledge, does the person still have the power (qudra) to disbelieve? The answer leads to absurdities either way. Then, the author delivers the final blow with a Quranic verse that explicitly states God does not guide every soul because of His decree to fill Hell. This lesson presents the culmination of the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
The author asks: after necessary knowledge, does the person have the power to disbelieve? Consider both answers.
2
Analyze each horn
If 'no', then command and punishment are unjust. If 'yes', then disbelief remains possible, contrary to the claim.
This shows the inconsistency in Abu Hashim's model.
3
Study the Quranic proof
Read the verse from Surah Al-Sajda. Understand how it conclusively shows that God's will determines guidance, not just knowledge.
The verse directly contradicts the idea that necessary knowledge forces faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما رأى ابنه أبو هاشم فساد كلام أبيه زعم أن معنى مشيئة الجبران أن يخلق الله تعالى لهم العلم الضروري أنهم لو لم يؤمنوا لعذبوا عذابًا شديدا. وهذا أيضا فاسد لأن أهل العناد كانوا يعلمون أنهم يخلدون في النار بتكذيبه عليه السلام وما كانوا يؤمنون، وإبليس يعلم بذلك ولا يؤمن، فكذا من قامت له الدلائل الموجبة للعلم أو الذي خلق له العلم الضروري يعلم بذلك ولا يؤمن. ثم المذهب عنده أن الله تعالى يقدر على الظلم والسفه والكذب، ولو فعل شيئًا من ذلك لبطلت ألوهيته، ولا ضرر أعظم من زوال الربوبية وصيرورته عبدًا مربوبًا معاقبًا وهو يعلم أنه لو ظلم أو كذب أو سفه لتزول ربوبيته فكان على قضية كلامه مجبوراً على العدل والصدق والحكمة. وقد قررت الكلام فيه في مسألة خلق الأفعال ثم يقال له ولأبيه: هل بقيت معه قدرة الكفر بعد العلم الضروري بصحة الإيمان أو العلم أنه يعاقب؟ فإن قال: لا، قيل: كيف يؤمر بترك كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ وكيف يؤمر بالإيمان بدون القدرة إذ لو كانت قدرة الإيمان موجودة لكانت هي بعينها قدرة الكفر؟ وكيف يعاقب على كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ فإن قال: نعم. قيل: إذا كنت قدرة الكفر موجودة كان من الجائز أن يكفر بها ولا يؤمن. ثم الذي يبطل جميع تأويلاتهم أن الله تعالى قال : وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا وَلَكِنْ حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِنِّي لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ أخبر أنه تعالى لم يأت كل نفس هداها لما أن حق القول منه الأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ ولو أتى كل نفس
When his son Abu Hashim saw the falsity of his father's statement, he claimed that the meaning of 'willing' of the jabrians is that God Most High creates for them necessary knowledge that if they do not believe, they will be punished with a severe punishment. This is also false, because the obstinate people knew that they would abide forever in the Fire due to their denial of him (peace be upon him) and they would not believe, and Iblis knows that and does not believe. So likewise, the one for whom proofs necessitating knowledge are established, or the one for whom necessary knowledge has been created, knows that and does not believe. Then, according to him, the doctrine is that God Most High has power over injustice, foolishness, and lying. If He did any of that, His divinity would be invalidated. And there is no greater harm than the removal of lordship and his becoming a subjugated, punishable servant, while he knows that if He were unjust, lied, or acted foolishly, His lordship would be removed. So, according to the implication of his statement, He would be compelled to justice, truth, and wisdom. I have already discussed this in the issue of the creation of actions. Then it is said to him and his father: Does the power of disbelief remain with him after the necessary knowledge of the soundness of faith, or the knowledge that he will be punished? If he says: No, it is said: How can he be commanded to abandon disbelief which he has no power over? And how can he be commanded to believe without power, since if the power of faith existed, it would be the same as the power of disbelief? And how can he be punished for disbelief over which he has no power? If he says: Yes, it is said: If the power of disbelief exists, it is possible that he disbelieves with it and does not believe. Then that which invalidates all their interpretations is that God Most High said: 'And if We had willed, We could have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me will be fulfilled: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.' He informed that He Most High does not give every soul its guidance because the word from Him is 'I will surely fill Hell.' And if He gave every soul...
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage refutes Abu Hashim's alternative interpretation of God's 'willing' regarding faith. Abu Hashim claimed that God's will means He creates necessary knowledge in the disbeliever that if he does not believe, he will be severely punished. The author declares this false by pointing out that obstinate people (like the People of the Book) already knew they would be in the Fire for denying the Prophet, yet they did not believe, and Iblis knows this but does not believe. So knowledge of punishment does not necessitate faith. Next, the author notes Abu Hashim's own doctrine: that God has power over injustice, lying, etc., but if He did so, His divinity would be invalidated. The author argues that on Abu Hashim's premise, God would be compelled (mujbar) to be just, wise, etc., which contradicts the idea of free will. Then the author raises a dilemma: after necessary knowledge, does the ability (qudra) to disbelieve remain? If not, how can God command to abandon disbelief or punish for it? If yes, then the person might still disbelieve. Finally, the author presents the decisive refutation: Quran 32:13, where God states that if He willed, He could guide every soul, but His decree is to fill Hell. Thus, God does not give guidance to everyone, proving that necessary knowledge or proof does not force faith.

الإيمان
القرآن
هدى
جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that necessary knowledge removes free will completely.
Correction: The dilemma shows that either the person still has the ability to choose (contradicting the compulsion claim) or not (making commands unjust). The Quran confirms God's will is decisive.

Checkpoint
What is the decisive proof the author offers to refute all interpretations?
A) The example of Iblis
B) The argument about God's power
C) Quran 32:13 about God not guiding every soul
D) The dilemma about power

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse conclusively shows that God's will, not merely knowledge, determines who is guided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The verse says God could guide everyone but does not. If you are among those He guides, how will you respond with gratitude today? If you are not, what excuse will you have on that Day?
?
The dilemma shows that commanding someone without ability is unjust. Do you believe you have the ability to obey every command of God? When you fail, do you blame your inability or your choice?
?
You now know that even with clear knowledge of truth, you could still choose disbelief. When have you experienced a moment of clear truth but still hesitated to act? What does that reveal about your heart's attachment?

Why Coercive Guidance Cannot Be from Allah
Author refutes coercive guidance and verifies voluntary faith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Allah guides people coercively to fill Hell is logically and theologically unsound.

Core Idea
Coercive faith cannot be what Allah intends because it does not yield reward or punishment.

The author begins by pointing out a key contradiction in the view that Allah forces people to believe and then punishes them. If someone is guided, they do not belong in Hell. Moreover, forcing guidance does not cancel their deservingness of punishment. This introduction sets the stage for a deeper verification of what kind of faith Allah actually wills.

Guided Path
1
Read and understand the passage
Read the Arabic slowly, noting the logical flow of the argument. Pay attention to the structure: first a contradiction, then a verification.
2
Identify the contradiction
Notice that the opponents' claim leads to an absurdity: the guided one fills Hell. The author says this indicates falsity.
3
Trace the verification argument
Follow the author's reasoning that coercive faith cannot be the faith that makes one deserving of Paradise. Therefore, it cannot be what Allah willed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هداها لم يتصور أن يملأ جهنم بهم لأن المهتدي لا يملأ به جهنم، وإعطاء الهدى بطريق الجبر على الطرق التي زعموا لا يخرجهم من استحقاقهم جهنم، وأن يملأ منهم جهنم، فدل أن هذا باطل. يحققه أن لو شاء إيمانهم بطريق الجبر على ما زعموا وحصل إيمانهم لما كان ذلك الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا هو الإيمان الذي شاء الله منهم؛ لأنه على زعمهم شاء منهم الإيمان الاختياري الذي يصيرون به مستحقين للجنة والثواب خارجين عن أن يكونوا أهلا للعقاب، وما يحصل من الإيمان بمشيئة الجبر لا يكون هذا الإيمان فإن العبد لا يصير به أهلاً للجنة والثواب ولا يخرج عن استحقاق العقاب على طريق التخليد، فإذا لم يبق قادرًا على تحصيل ما أراد في ملكه وغلبت مشيئته مشيئة إبليس وإرادة كل كافر، ولأنه لا معنى لتعلق الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا بالمشيئة والإخبار أنه لو شاء لفعل لأنه قد فعل ذلك وحصل من كل كافر إذ كل كافر وكل مخلوق يشهد بخلقه أن له صانعا حكيمًا عليمًا موصوفا بصفات الكمال متبرئًا عن سمات النقص لا يؤيد بالمعجزة الكاذب، ولا يقيم دلالة الصدق على دعوى المفتري، فكان على هذا كل مخلوق مؤمنًا بخلقته، وقد شاء الله تعالى ذلك وفعل لا معنى لقوله (وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ) وقوله (وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا)، وقد فعل ذلك فدل أن المراد من الآية ليس هو الإيمان الحاصل جبرا بل إيمانهم الاختياري، وقد صح في المروي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه كان يقول: 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' وكذا هذه اللفظة متداولة على ألسنة الأمة ولا وجه لحملها على مشيئة الجبر؛ لأنه لو استقام بأحد شطري الكلام لم يستقم بالشطر الآخر فإنه إن أمكن أن يقال: ما شاء الله جبراً كأن لم يمكن أن يقال وما لم يشأ جبرًا لم يكن، لأن الطاعات كلها عندكم لم يشأ جبرًا وكانت والمعاصي لم يشأ جبرًا، وقد كانت فدل أن المراد من المشيئة غير مشيئة الجبر.
He guided them cannot be imagined that He would fill Hell with them because the guided one does not fill Hell with him, and giving guidance by way of coercion on the paths they claimed does not remove them from their deservingness of Hell, and that He would fill Hell with them, so this indicates that this is false. He verifies: If He willed their faith by way of coercion according to what they claimed and their faith occurred, that faith occurring by coercion would not be the faith that God willed from them; because according to their claim, He willed from them voluntary faith by which they become deserving of Paradise and reward, being excluded from being worthy of punishment, and what occurs of faith by the will of coercion is not this faith, for the servant does not become by it deserving of Paradise and reward nor does he exit from deservingness of punishment in the way of eternal [punishment]. So when He is not able to accomplish what He desired in His kingdom and His will is overcome by the will of Iblis and the will of every disbeliever, and because there is no meaning to attaching the faith that occurs by coercion to the will and the information that if He willed He would do [it] because He has done that and it occurred from every disbeliever, since every disbeliever and every creature bears witness by his creation that he has a wise, knowing Creator described with attributes of perfection, free from marks of deficiency, who does not support the liar with a miracle, nor does He establish evidence of truthfulness upon the claim of the fabricator. So on this basis, every creature is a believer by his creation, and God Almighty willed that and did it, so there is no meaning to His saying: 'And if your Lord had willed, whoever is on the earth would have believed' and His saying: 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' and He has done that. So it indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not the faith that occurs by coercion but rather their voluntary faith. And it is established in the transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to say: 'What God wills occurs and what He does not will does not occur.' And likewise this phrase is common on the tongues of the community, and there is no way to interpret it as the will of coercion; because if it were sound with one part of the statement, it would not be sound with the other part. For if it could be said: 'What God wills by coercion is' it could not be said: 'And what He does not will by coercion is not', because acts of obedience according to you He did not will by coercion and they occurred, and acts of disobedience He did not will by coercion and they occurred. So it indicates that the intended meaning of will is other than the will of coercion.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a proof that divine will for faith is voluntary, not coercive. The author begins by stating that the claim that God gives guidance coercively to fill Hell is false because the guided one does not fill Hell. Then he verifies: if God willed their faith coercively, that faith would not be the faith He intended, which is voluntary faith that makes one deserving of paradise. Coercive faith does not make one deserving of paradise or exempt from punishment. If God were unable to achieve His will against Iblis's will, that would be problematic. Further, every creature by nature recognizes God, so if God willed faith coercively, all would believe, but that contradicts the Quranic verses that indicate not all believe. The hadith 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' is interpreted as referring to the will of command (voluntary) not coercive will, because if it were coercive, it would not hold for both parts: God does not will obedience coercively yet it occurs, and does not will disobedience coercively yet it occurs. Thus the will in the hadith is not coercive will.

Key Terms
الجبر
الإيمان الاختياري
الهدى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah forces people to believe and then punishes them for not believing.
Correction: The author shows this is contradictory because forced guidance would not lead to deserving punishment, and the faith that results from coercion is not the faith that makes one deserving of Paradise.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does coercive guidance not fulfill Allah's intention?
A) It is impossible for Allah to do so.
B) The resulting faith does not make one deserving of Paradise.
C) It would mean all are guided.
D) The Prophet forbade it.

Key Takeaway
Coercive faith cannot be the faith Allah wills because it does not result in the reward of Paradise or exemption from punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself acting like your faith is something forced upon you, blaming circumstances or destiny for your lack of sincerity? If so, how will you reclaim the voluntary nature of your faith starting today?
?
This lesson argues that coercive faith does not remove deservingness of punishment. If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow, would you rather your faith be a coerced act that excuses nothing, or a voluntary choice that He can reward? What one step will you take to ensure your faith is truly voluntary?
?
The passage shows that Allah wills voluntary faith from you. Are there areas of your life where you are passively waiting for Allah to 'guide' you by force, instead of actively seeking Him with your free will? Write down one specific area where you will choose to act voluntarily this week.

Interpreting Divine Will: Voluntary Not Coercive
Author interprets Quran and hadith regarding divine will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author interprets Quranic verses and the prophetic hadith to show that Allah's will for faith is voluntary.

Core Idea
When Allah says 'If We willed, We would have guided every soul', He means voluntary guidance, not coercion.

After establishing that coercive faith is not what Allah intends, the author addresses potential proof texts that opponents might cite. He demonstrates that the Quranic verses about Allah's will and the famous hadith 'ما شاء الله كان' must be understood as referring to voluntary will, not coercive will, because a coercive interpretation leads to absurd consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Focus on how the author uses the universal belief by creation and the Quranic verses. Notice the structure: argument from inability, argument from creation, Quranic verses, and hadith.
2
Analyze the argument from creation
Note the claim that every creature bears witness to its Creator, so if will were coercive, all would believe. But we see disbelievers, so the verses must refer to voluntary faith.
3
Examine the hadith interpretation
See how the author argues that the hadith cannot refer to coercive will because both obedience and disobedience occur without being willed coercively.

So it indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not the faith that occurs by coercion but rather their voluntary faith. And it is established in the transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to say: 'What God wills occurs and what He does not will does not occur.' And likewise this phrase is common on the tongues of the community, and there is no way to interpret it as the will of coercion; because if it were sound with one part of the statement, it would not be sound with the other part. For if it could be said: 'What God wills by coercion is' it could not be said: 'And what He does not will by coercion is not', because acts of obedience according to you He did not will by coercion and they occurred, and acts of disobedience He did not will by coercion and they occurred. So it indicates that the intended meaning of will is other than the will of coercion.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a proof that divine will for faith is voluntary, not coercive. The author begins by stating that the claim that God gives guidance coercively to fill Hell is false because the guided one does not fill Hell. Then he verifies: if God willed their faith coercively, that faith would not be the faith He intended, which is voluntary faith that makes one deserving of paradise. Coercive faith does not make one deserving of paradise or exempt from punishment. If God were unable to achieve His will against Iblis's will, that would be problematic. Further, every creature by nature recognizes God, so if God willed faith coercively, all would believe, but that contradicts the Quranic verses that indicate not all believe. The hadith 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' is interpreted as referring to the will of command (voluntary) not coercive will, because if it were coercive, it would not hold for both parts: God does not will obedience coercively yet it occurs, and does not will disobedience coercively yet it occurs. Thus the will in the hadith is not coercive will.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الجبر
الإيمان الاختياري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'ما شاء الله كان' proves coercive will.
Correction: The author shows it would lead to absurdity because both obedience and disobedience occur without being willed coercively.

Checkpoint
How does the author argue against interpreting the hadith 'ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن' as coercive will?
A) Because it is not found in the Quran.
B) Because if it were coercive, then what Allah does not will coercively would not occur, yet obedience and disobedience occur.
C) Because the Prophet said it.
D) Because it contradicts other hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses and the prophetic hadith about Allah's will must be understood as referring to voluntary guidance, not coercive, otherwise they lead to absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's guidance is voluntary and you are free to choose, what does your current level of faith reveal about your response to His call? Are you truly seeking Him, or have you become comfortable in negligence?
?
Every creature bears witness to its Creator, but you might have ignored that inner testimony. What would change today if you finally heeded that witness and submitted your will wholeheartedly?
?
The hadith says 'What God wills occurs'—yet your obedience and disobedience are your own choices. Does this truth make you more accountable for your actions? How will you live differently knowing that your faith is not forced but a gift you must actively embrace?

Proof that Collective Guidance Cannot Be Coercive
Proves from Quran 6:35 that coercive guidance is not intended.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'ولو شاء الله لجمعهم على الهدى' demonstrates that God's intended guidance is voluntary, not coercive.

Core Idea
Coercive guidance cannot save; true guidance must be voluntary.

The author uses a key Quranic verse to argue that if God intended to gather all people upon guidance, that guidance must be of a single saving type. Since coercive guidance does not lead to Paradise, it cannot be the guidance meant. This leads to the conclusion that God did not will the voluntary faith of disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic verse and its translation. Notice that God says 'if He willed, He would gather them upon guidance'.
The verse is from Surah Al-An'am (6:35).
2
Identify the two types of guidance
The author distinguishes between coercive guidance (هدى جبر) and voluntary guidance (هدى اختيار). Coercive guidance does not lead to salvation, voluntary does.
3
Understand the two possible ways to gather all
To gather all on guidance, either disbelievers must accept voluntarily, or believers must be forced to coercive guidance. The second option is unjust and not wise.
The author enumerates these two possibilities.
4
See why force is not wisdom
Forcing believers away from voluntary faith is not from wisdom. So the only valid interpretation is that God did not will the voluntary faith of disbelievers.
5
Conclusion: God's will for guidance is voluntary
Thus, the verse proves that God did not will the voluntary faith of disbelievers, and that His will for guidance is only for those who believe by choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أنه تعالى قال: (وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ لَجَمَعَهُمْ عَلَى الْهُدَى). وإنما يكون جمعهم على الهدى أن لو كان هدى الكل جنساً واحدًا فأما إذا كان هدى البعض جبرًا ولا تنال به الجنة، ولا يتخلص به عن النار وهدى البعض اختيارا، وتنال به الجنة ويتخلص به عن النار فلا يكون هذا جمعهم على الهدى وهو يكون بأحد وجهين إما أن يهدي الكفار باختيارهم حتى يكونوا مع الذين آمنوا باختيارهم مجموعين على الهدى، وإما أن يخلق الاهتداء جبرًا في الكفار ومنع الذين اهتدوا باختيارهم عن الهدى الاختياري وأثبت فيهم الهدى بطريق الجبر، وهذا منه صرف للمؤمنين عن الإيمان قهرا وجبرا، وهذا ليس بحكمة فلم يبق إلا أن يكون المراد هو جمع الكل على الهدى وهو ما بينا، فإذا لم يشأ ذلك دل أنه لم يشأ إيمان الكفرة، والله الموفق.
He verifies: God Almighty said: 'And if God had willed, He would have gathered them upon guidance.' And His gathering them upon guidance would only be if the guidance of all was one type. But if the guidance of some is by coercion and they do not attain Paradise by it, nor are they saved from the Fire, and the guidance of others is voluntary, and they attain Paradise by it and are saved from the Fire, then this is not gathering them upon guidance. And it would be in one of two ways: either that He guides the disbelievers by their choice so that they are together with those who believed by their choice, gathered upon guidance; or that He creates guidance by coercion in the disbelievers and prevents those who were guided by their choice from voluntary guidance and establishes in them guidance by way of coercion. And this is from Him a turning away of the believers from faith by force and coercion, and this is not wisdom. So nothing remains except that the intended meaning is gathering all upon guidance, which is what we explained. So when He did not will that, it indicates that He did not will the faith of the disbelievers. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a proof from Quran 6:35 that God's will for guidance is not coercive. The verse says if God willed, He would gather all on guidance. The author argues that gathering all on guidance would require guidance to be of one type. If some have coercive guidance (which does not lead to Paradise or save from Hell) and others have voluntary guidance (which does), then gathering is not achieved. The only two ways to gather all would be either to guide disbelievers voluntarily so they join believers, or to force believers into coercive guidance—which is unjust and not wise. Since God did not do either, it means He did not will the faith of disbelievers (voluntarily); He only wills it for those who believe.

Key Terms
الهدى
الجبر
الاختيار
الجميع على الهدى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that if God willed guidance for all, He would force everyone to be guided.
Correction: Forced guidance does not lead to salvation, so it cannot be the guidance meant by 'gathering upon guidance'. True guidance must be voluntary to be saving.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the verse 'ولو شاء الله لجمعهم على الهدى' prove that God did not will the faith of disbelievers?
A) Because if He willed it, He would have forced them, but He didn't
B) Because gathering all on guidance requires a single kind of guidance, and coercive guidance does not achieve salvation
C) Because the verse only applies to believers
D) Because God's will is limited

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse proves that God's will for guidance is not coercive, because forced guidance does not save, so only voluntary faith is intended for believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Does your faith feel like a forced routine or a voluntary response to God's guidance? What would change if you truly owned your iman as a personal choice?
?

?
This lesson shows that coerced faith does not save. Is there any area of your life where you are pretending to believe but your heart is not truly submitted? What will you do about it today?
